Two pairs of small stagnant ice bodies on the Hazen Plateau of northeastern Ellesmere Island, the St. Patrick Bay ice caps and the Murray and Simmons ice caps, are rapidly shrinking, and the remnants of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps are likely to disappear entirely within the next 5 years. Vertical aerial photographs of these Little Ice Age relics taken during August of 1959 show that the larger of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps had an area of 7.48\u202fkm2 and the smaller one 2.93\u202fkm2; the Murray and Simmons ice caps covered 4.37 and 7.45\u202fkm2 respectively. Outlines determined from ASTER satellite data for July 2016 show that, compared to 1959, the larger and the smaller of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps had both been reduced to only 5\u202f% of their former area, with the Murray and Simmons ice caps faring better at 39 and 25\u202f%, likely reflecting their higher elevation. Consistent with findings from other glaciological studies in the Queen Elizabeth Islands, ASTER imagery in conjunction with past GPS surveys documents a strikingly rapid wastage of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps over the last 15\u00a0years. These two ice caps shrank noticeably even between 2014 and 2015, apparently in direct response to the especially warm summer of 2015 over northeastern Ellesmere Island. The well-documented recession patterns of the Hazen Plateau ice caps over the last 55+ years offer an opportunity to examine the processes of plant recolonization of polar landscapes.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tc-11-169-2017", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2017, 1, 25]], "date-time": "2017-01-25T08:31:34Z", "timestamp": 1485333094000}, "page": "169-177", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 1, "title": ["Rapid wastage of the Hazen Plateau ice caps, northeastern Ellesmere Island, Nunavut, Canada"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "11", "author": [{"given": "Mark C.", "family": "Serreze", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Bruce", "family": "Raup", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Carsten", "family": "Braun", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Douglas R.", "family": "Hardy", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0002-4032-9519", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "Raymond S.", "family": "Bradley", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "3145", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2017, 1, 25]]}, "reference": [{"key": "ref1", "unstructured": "Alt, B.: Synoptic climate controls of mass balance variations on Devon Island Ice Cap, Arc. "timestamp": 1473379200000}, "delay-in-days": 0, "content-version": "unspecified"}], "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "abstract": "<jats:p>&amp;lt;p&amp;gt;&amp;lt;strong&amp;gt;Abstract.&amp;lt;/strong&amp;gt; Two pairs of small stagnant ice bodies on the Hazen Plateau of northeastern Ellesmere Island, the St.&amp;amp;#160;Patrick Bay ice caps and the Murray and Simmons ice caps, are rapidly shrinking, and the remnants of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps are likely to disappear entirely within the next five years. Vertical aerial photographs of these Little Ice Age relics taken during August of 1959 show that the larger of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps had an area of 7.48&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;, and the smaller one 2.93&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;. The Murray and Simmons ice caps covered 4.37&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; and 7.45&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; respectively. Outlines determined from ASTER satellite data for July 2016 show that, compared to 1959, the larger and the smaller of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps had both been reduced to only 5&amp;amp;#8201;% of their former area, with the Murray and Simmons ice caps faring better at 39&amp;amp;#8201;% and 25&amp;amp;#8201;%, likely reflecting their higher elevation. ASTER imagery in conjunction with past GPS surveys documents a strikingly rapid wastage of the St. Patrick Bay ice caps over the last 15 years. These two ice caps shrank noticeably even between 2014 and 2015, apparently in direct response to the especially warm summer of 2015 over northeastern Ellesmere Island. The well-documented recession patterns of the Hazen Plateau ice caps over the last 55+ years offer an opportunity to examine the processes of plant recolonization of polar landscapes.&amp;lt;/p&amp;gt;\n                        </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tc-2016-201", "type": "posted-content", "created": {"date-parts": [[2016, 9, 9]], "date-time": "content-version": "unspecified"}], "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "short-container-title": ["The Cryosphere"], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. Due to their remoteness, altitude and harsh climatic conditions, little is known about the glaciological parameters of ice caps on the Tibetan Plateau. This study presents a geodetic mass balance estimate of the Purogangri Ice Cap, Tibet's largest ice field between 2000 and 2012. We utilized data from the actual TerraSAR-X mission and its add-on for digital elevation measurements and compared it with elevation data from the Shuttle Radar Topography Mission. The employed data sets are ideal for this approach as both data sets were acquired at X-band at nearly the same time of the year and are available at a fine grid spacing. In order to derive surface elevation changes we employed two different methods. The first method is based on differential synthetic radar interferometry while the second method uses common DEM differencing. Both approaches revealed a slightly negative mass budget of \u221244 \u00b1 15 and \u221238 \u00b1 23 mm w.eq. a\u22121 (millimeter water equivalent) respectively. A slightly negative trend of \u22120.15 \u00b1 0.01 km2 a\u22121 in glacier extent was found for the same time period employing a time series of Landsat data. Overall, our results show an almost balanced mass budget for the studied time period. Additionally, we detected one continuously advancing glacier tongue in the eastern part of the ice cap.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tc-7-1623-2013", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2013, 10, 24]], "date-time": "2013-10-24T08:52:19Z", "timestamp": 1382604739000}, "page": "1623-1633", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 39, "title": ["Recent mass balance of the Purogangri Ice Cap, central Tibetan Plateau, by means of differential X-band SAR interferometry"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "7", "author": [{"given": "N.", "family": "Neckel", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0001-8630-1389", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "A.", "family": "Braun", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "J.", "family": "Krop\u00e1\u010dek", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "V.", "family": "Hochschild", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "3145", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2013, 10, 24]]}, "reference": [{"key": "ref1", "unstructured": "Arendt et al.: Randolph Glacier Inventory [v2.0]: A Dataset of Global Glacier Outlines. Due to their remoteness, altitude and harsh climatic conditions, little is known about the glaciological parameters of ice caps on the Tibetan Plateau (TP). This study presents an interferometrical approach aiming at surface elevation changes of Purogangri ice cap, located on the central TP. Purogangri ice cap covers an area of 397 \u00b1 9.7 km2 and is the largest ice cap on the TP. Its behavior is determined by dry and cold continental climate suggesting a polar-type glacier regime. We employed data from the actual TerraSAR-X mission and its add-on for Digital Elevation Measurements (TanDEM-X) and compare it with elevation data from the Shuttle Radar Topography Mission (SRTM). These datasets are ideal for this approach as both datasets feature the same wavelength of 3.1 cm and are available at a fine grid spacing. Similar snow conditions can be assumed since the data were acquired in early February 2000 and late January 2012. The trend in glacier extend was extracted using a time series of Landsat data. Our results show a balanced mass budget for the studied time period which is in agreement with previous studies. Additionally, we detected an exceptional fast advance of one glacier tongue in the eastern part of the ice cap between 1999 and 2011.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tcd-7-1119-2013", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2013, 3, 21]], "date-time": "2013-03-21T13:18:20Z", "timestamp": 1363871900000}, "page": "1119-1139", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 1, "title": ["Recent mass balance of Purogangri ice cap, central Tibetan Plateau, by means of differential X-band SAR interferometry"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "7", "author": [{"given": "N.", "family": "Neckel", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0001-8630-1389", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "A.", "family": "Braun", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "J.", "family": "Krop\u00e1\u010dek", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "V.", "family": "Hochschild", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "3145", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2013, 3, 21]]}, "reference": [{"key": "ref1", "unstructured": "Bader, H.: Sorge's law of densification of snow on high polar glaciers, J. "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "short-container-title": ["The Cryosphere"], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. Glaciers in tropical regions are very sensitive to\nclimatic variations and thus strongly affected by climate change. The\nmajority of the tropical glaciers worldwide are located in the Peruvian\nAndes, which have shown significant ice loss in the last century. Here, we\npresent the first multi-temporal, region-wide survey of geodetic mass\nbalances and glacier area fluctuations throughout Peru covering the period\n2000\u20132016. Glacier extents are derived from Landsat imagery by performing\nautomatic glacier delineation based on a combination of the NDSI and band\nratio method and final manual inspection and correction. The mapping of\ndebris-covered glacier extents is supported by synthetic aperture radar (SAR) coherence information. A\ntotal glacier area loss of -548.5\u00b165.7\u2009km2 (\u221229\u2009%,\n\u221234.3\u2009km2\u2009a\u22121) is obtained for the study period. Using\ninterferometric satellite SAR acquisitions, bi-temporal geodetic mass\nbalances are derived. An average specific mass balance of -296\u00b141\u2009kg\u2009m\u22122\u2009a\u22121 is found throughout Peru for the period 2000\u20132016.\nHowever, there are strong regional and temporal differences in the mass\nbudgets ranging from 45\u00b197 to -752\u00b1452\u2009kg\u2009m\u22122\u2009a\u22121. The ice loss increased towards the end of the observation\nperiod. Between 2013 and 2016, a retreat of the glacierized area of\n-203.8\u00b165.7\u2009km2 (\u221216\u2009%, \u2212101.9\u2009km2\u2009a\u22121) is mapped and the average mass budget amounts to -660\u00b1178\u2009kg\u2009m\u22122\u2009a\u22121. The glacier changes revealed can be attributed to\nchanges in the climatic settings in the study region, derived from\nERA-Interim reanalysis data and the Oceanic Nino Index. The intense El\nNi\u00f1o activities in 2015/16 are most likely the trigger for the increased\nchange rates in the time interval 2013\u20132016. Our observations provide\nfundamental information on the current dramatic glacier changes for local\nauthorities and for the calibration and validation of glacier change\nprojections.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tc-13-2537-2019", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2019, 9, 30]], "date-time": "2019-09-30T14:14:43Z", "timestamp": 1569852883000}, "page": "2537-2556", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 0, "title": ["Changes of the tropical glaciers throughout Peru between 2000 and 2016 \u2013 mass balance and area fluctuations"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "13", "author": [{"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0001-5055-8959", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "Thorsten", "family": "Seehaus", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0001-7787-2948", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "Philipp", "family": "Malz", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Christian", "family": "Sommer", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0003-0312-0051", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "Stefan", "family": "Lippl", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Alejo", "family": "Cochachin", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Matthias", "family": "Braun", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "3145", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2019, 9, 30]]}, "reference": [{"key": "ref1", "unstructured": "Atwood, D. "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "abstract": "<jats:p>&amp;lt;p&amp;gt;&amp;lt;strong&amp;gt;Abstract.&amp;lt;/strong&amp;gt; Glaciers in tropical regions are very sensitive to climatic variations and thus strongly affected by climate change. The majority of the tropical glaciers worldwide are located in the Peruvian Andes, which have shown significant ice loss in the last century. Here, we present the first multi-temporal, region wide survey of geodetic mass balances and glacier area fluctuations throughout Peru covering the period 2000&amp;amp;#8211;2016. Glacier extents are derived from Landsat imagery by performing automatic glacier delineation based on a combination of the NDSI and band ratio method and final manual inspection and correction. A total glacier area loss of &amp;amp;#8722;548.5&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;65.7&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; (&amp;amp;#8722;29&amp;amp;#8201;%, &amp;amp;#8722;34.3&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;) is obtained for the study period. Using interferometric satellite SAR acquisitions, bi-temporal geodetic mass balances are derived. An average specific mass balance of &amp;amp;#8722;357&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;43&amp;amp;#8201;kg&amp;amp;#8201;m&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; is found throughout Peru for the period 2000&amp;amp;#8211;2016. However, there are strong regional and temporal differences in the mass budgets ranging from 68&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;102&amp;amp;#8201;kg&amp;amp;#8201;m&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; to &amp;amp;#8722;990&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;476&amp;amp;#8201;kg&amp;amp;#8201;m&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;. The ice loss increased towards the end of the observation period. Between 2013 and 2016, a retreat of the glaciated area of &amp;amp;#8722;203.8&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;65.7&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt; (&amp;amp;#8722;&amp;amp;#8201;16&amp;amp;#8201;%, &amp;amp;#8722;101.9&amp;amp;#8201;km&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;) is mapped and the average mass budget amounts to &amp;amp;#8722;836&amp;amp;#8201;&amp;amp;#177;&amp;amp;#8201;188&amp;amp;#8201;kg&amp;amp;#8201;m&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;2&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8201;a&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;&amp;amp;#8722;1&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;. The glacier changes revealed can be attributed to changes in the climatic settings in the study region, derived from ERA-Interim reanalysis data and the Oceanic Ni&amp;amp;#241;o Index. The intense El Ni&amp;amp;#241;o activities in 2015/16 are most likely the trigger for the increased change rates in the time interval 2013&amp;amp;#8211;2016. Our observations provide fundamental information on the current dramatic glacier changes for local authorities and for the calibration and validation of glacier change projections.&amp;lt;/p&amp;gt;\n Glaciol."], "published-print": {"date-parts": [[2013]]}, "abstract": "<jats:title>Abstract</jats:title><jats:p>Vestfonna ice cap, northeastern Svalbard, is one of the largest ice bodies in the European Arctic, but little is known about the evolution of its mass balance. This study presents a reconstruction of the climatic mass balance of the ice cap for the period 1979/80-2010/11. The reconstruction is based on calculations using a mass-balance model that combines a surface-elevation-dependent accumulation scheme with a spatially distributed temperature-index ablation model that includes net shortwave radiation. Refreezing is included, based on the basic <jats:italic>P</jats:italic><jats:sub>max</jats:sub> approach. The model accounts for cloud-cover effects and surface albedo variations that are calculated by a statistical albedo model. ERA-Interim derived air temperature, precipitation and total cloud-cover data are used as input. Results reveal a mean climatic mass-balance rate of +0.09 \u00b1 0.15 m w.e. a<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup> for the study period. Annual balances show a slight, insignificant trend towards less positive values over the study period. Refreezing is estimated to contribute about one-third to annual accumulation, and a significant positive trend in refreezing is present over the study period. The modelling results reveal a significant steepening of the climatic mass-balance gradient and indicate a lengthening of the characteristic 3 month ablation period in recent years.</jats:p>", "DOI": "<jats:p>Abstract. The mass budget of the ice caps surrounding the Antarctica Peninsula and, in particular, the partitioning of its main components are poorly known. Here we approximate frontal ablation (i.e. the sum of mass losses by calving and submarine melt) and surface mass balance of the ice cap of Livingston Island, the second largest island in the South Shetland Islands archipelago, and analyse variations in surface velocity for the period 2007\u20132011. Velocities are obtained from feature tracking using 25 PALSAR-1 images, and used in conjunction with estimates of glacier ice thicknesses inferred from principles of glacier dynamics and ground-penetrating radar observations to estimate frontal ablation rates by a flux-gate approach. Glacier-wide surface mass-balance rates are approximated from in situ observations on two glaciers of the ice cap. Within the limitations of the large uncertainties mostly due to unknown ice thicknesses at the flux gates, we find that frontal ablation (\u2212509 \u00b1 263 Mt yr\u22121, equivalent to \u22120.73 \u00b1 0.38 m w.e. yr\u22121 over the ice cap area of 697 km2) and surface ablation (\u22120.73 \u00b1 0.10 m w.e. yr\u22121) contribute similar shares to total ablation (\u22121.46 \u00b1 0.39 m w.e. yr\u22121). Total mass change (\u03b4M = \u22120.67 &amp;amp;plusmn 0.40 m w.e. yr\u22121) is negative despite a slightly positive surface mass balance (0.06 \u00b1 0.14 m w.e. yr\u22121). We find large interannual and, for some basins, pronounced seasonal variations in surface velocities at the flux gates, with higher velocities in summer than in winter. Associated variations in frontal ablation (of ~237 Mt yr\u22121; \u22120.34 m w.e. yr\u22121) highlight the importance of taking into account the seasonality in ice velocities when computing frontal ablation with a flux-gate approach.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/tc-8-1807-2014", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2014, 10, 8]], "date-time": "2014-10-08T06:23:03Z", "timestamp": 1412749383000}, "page": "1807-1823", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 23, "title": ["Surface velocity and mass balance of Livingston Island ice cap, Antarctica"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "8", "author": [{"given": "B.", "family": "Osmanoglu", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0002-5147-0067", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "F.
